Page 14

Opinions of the Bureau of Commodity Inspection on the Trial Planting of Indian Tea 123

The Ministry's Approval of the Proposed Methods

The Shanghai Bureau of Commodity Inspection previously received instructions from the Ministry of Industry, following a communication from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, regarding the request from Tao Yin, the Vice-Consul at the Consulate in Liverpool, to improve tea leaves and promote international trade, as previously reported in the newspaper. Now, the Bureau believes that there are debatable points in Vice-Consul Tao's proposed methods for trial planting Indian tea. Therefore, it has specifically drafted opinions and submitted them to the Ministry of Industry for instructions. Yesterday, it received approval from the Ministry, stating that the proposed methods are appropriate and instructing them to purchase tea seeds for trial planting promptly. The original submission and the Ministry's instructions are recorded below:

(Original Submission) Regarding the matter of submitting a report: We have received instruction No. 17131 from your ministry, stating that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has communicated, etc. Attached to this instruction is a copy of the original submission. Upon receiving this, we have reviewed the points made by Tao Yin, Vice-Consul at the Consulate in Liverpool, which are quite detailed, and the trial planting of Indian tea seems feasible. However, we have found that the main reasons for the annual decline in the export of Chinese tea are the complexity of tea garden varieties, the age of the trees, and poor manufacturing methods. In view of this, this Bureau has specifically joined the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute and the Hankou Bureau of Commodity Inspection this year in submitting a request to your ministry to establish a tea improvement farm in Ningzhou, Jiangxi Province. This is currently being planned, and a thorough study of various aspects of planting and manufacturing will be conducted. In one or two years, considerable results should be achieved. If Indian tea is promoted for planting immediately, not only will it be difficult for farmers to imitate, but also, due to poor manufacturing methods and the climate and soil, the effectiveness of foreign varieties is uncertain. We now propose the following methods for trial planting Indian tea: please first have your ministry specifically consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct consuls in India and Ceylon to collect dozens of varieties of tea seeds and distribute them to the Ningzhou Tea Improvement Farm, the Anhui and Hunan Tea Experiment Farms, and agricultural agencies in various regions for initial trial planting. After four or five years, trial manufacture should be conducted according to Indian and Ceylon tea manufacturing methods. If it is indeed superior to Chinese varieties, then suitable land should be selected for distribution to the public for imitation planting. Although this method may take more time, it is more reliable and seems to be a necessary step in propagating new varieties. Before receiving these instructions, we have informed various tea merchants so that those who are interested can conduct their own research and trial planting. We hereby submit these methods for proceeding with the planting of Indian tea to your ministry for review and approval. Please make a decision and implement accordingly. (Respectfully submitted).

(Ministry's Reply) We have received your submission. After reviewing it, we find the proposed methods appropriate. We have already consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct the consulates in Calcutta to investigate the prices and shipping costs of Indian and Ceylon tea seeds and the procedures for mail-order purchase, so that the tea farms can be informed and purchase seeds for trial planting as appropriate. You are hereby notified.

Municipal Zoo to Hold Animal Competitions 124

(Expansion of the Zoo Site Can Be Realized)

Seeking Donations and Foster Care of Animals (Since the Shanghai Municipal Zoo opened on the first of this month, it has been extremely crowded with visitors, averaging over 10,000 people per day. Ticket revenue is approximately 140 to 150 yuan per day. We are now exploring various news about the zoo, which is divided and recorded below.)

(Planning to Expand the Zoo Grounds)

Since the opening of the zoo, the number of visitors has been surprisingly high, making the zoo grounds feel quite small, and the zoo paths need to be widened. Therefore, expansion is being planned. Recently, contact has been made to purchase the Wei family cemetery behind the zoo at a negotiated price, which is likely to be successful. In addition, there are dozens of houses behind the zoo, which are public properties and can also be demolished in the future to expand the zoo grounds. With the current space, even if there is money to purchase other exotic animals, there is no space available for placement.

(Encouraging Donations and Foster Care) In order to increase the variety of animals, the zoo is specifically soliciting donations or foster care from the public and private sectors and has established reward regulations. Those who donate animals worth more than two yuan will receive entrance tickets or annual passes, and nameplates will be erected in the zoo to commemorate their contributions. Those who donate animals of great value may also have their names published in the newspaper to express gratitude. Those who donate animals worth less than two yuan will also receive entrance tickets.

(Holding Animal Competitions)

Currently, the zoo intends to hold various animal competitions or exhibitions to arouse public interest. The competitions that are currently being negotiated and prepared are the Frisian canary competition, for which prizes have been prepared for the winning bird owners. In addition, a specimen room has been opened, and some self-made specimens of dead snakes, monkeys, bears, roe deer, etc., are displayed. An order has been placed with 邏定 for a giant elephant. Plans are underway to open an aquarium, etc. As for the required funds, it is proposed that the daily ticket revenue be submitted to the Municipal Education Bureau and designated specifically for expansion.

(Early Cutoff for Ticket Sales) The zoo's opening hours are stipulated to be from morning to 12:00 noon and from afternoon to 6:00 pm. However, to ensure timely closure, the ticket sales time is cut off half an hour early, at 11:30 am and 5:30 pm, after which no entry is allowed. However, people who are unaware of this often arrive late, making the trip in vain.

(Statement on Feeding Tigers) Yesterday morning, the zoo received a letter from the China Animal Protection Association stating that it had been reported that live pigeons were being skinned and fed to tigers, and requesting that this be prohibited. According to Director Shen, this is not accurate. The lions, tigers, leopards, etc., in this zoo are fed beef every day. However, to adjust their nutritional intake, they are fed chicken once a week, but not live. The chickens are killed first, cut into pieces, and then provided. However, recently, it has been found that the chickens have a plague, and there are concerns about the impact, so pigeons were fed instead last Wednesday. The pigeons were first suffocated with a small string around their mouths, plucked, and then fed. However, on that day, one pigeon was not suffocated thoroughly and revived after death, leading to this incident. However, this was only seen by some. Attention will be paid to this in the future. This intention has been conveyed to the Association in a letter. The zoo welcomes suggestions from the outside world to improve operations.

Expressions of European Buddhists After Coming to China 125

"A Revolutionary China Can Save the World. Reliance on the League of Nations is Futile; Salvation Depends on Oneself." (Xin Xin News Agency) Ten Buddhists from France, Germany, Italy, Belgium, and other countries, including Bira, Apollo, Sitiputuo, Upala, Anukung Baijia, Patida, Patila Fa, Niaofa Ba, Shashipu, and Darubi, arrived in Shanghai on the Italian ship Conte Rosso on the 25th of last month. They were received by their teacher, Monk Zhaokong, and resided at 131 Da Xi Road. They plan to study Chinese for two years and then go to Baohua Mountain in Nanjing to receive ordination and take refuge in the Three Jewels. This has already been reported. It is now known that Monk Zhaokong and Bira, etc., came to Shanghai to become monks out of admiration for Eastern culture. They noted that China, despite its national difficulties, still maintains the virtues of tolerance and peace and a genuine inner civilization, which is truly commendable. Therefore, they drafted a letter titled "Monk Zhaokong and European Buddhists Coming to China to the Chinese People," which describes the comparison between Chinese and Western cultures in great detail. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency has translated the original text below:

(Advocating Peace) We, foreign Buddhist disciples, the first group, have arrived in two groups on the compassionate and welcoming shores of China. I will now, in my name and in the name of my disciples, express our sentiments to China and the Chinese people. First and foremost, I must express our deepest gratitude to you. Europe is a world of exaggeration, arrogance, deceit, injustice, depravity, and materialism. Their policy towards us peaceful Chinese Buddhist monks is no different from their previous treatment of China. Instead of relying on responsible government agencies, they rely on irresponsible individuals who bring their Christian (!) gunboats and various methods of pseudo-holy Christian governments to extort and seize vast amounts of Chinese land. If we were to invent a poisonous method that could kill 500,000 people in five seconds and take it back to Europe, we would surely receive enthusiastic cheers and various honors, and countless amounts of money would fall before us. However, my return to Europe would be as a lowly Buddhist monk. I advocate for peace. My sympathy lies with all of humanity. We gather people from various countries, sincerely and selflessly, loving each other and living in peace. This is something that those lying politicians and dishonest conferences cannot do and cannot tolerate in so-called progressive and civilized Europe. This is unmistakable proof that all truth, justice, and honesty have been declared bankrupt.

(China Saves the World) I am now returning to China, accompanied by men and women of loyalty and sincerity. They are all willing to follow the path of enlightenment and take refuge in the Buddha's teachings. Although China is currently in a state of turmoil, it still maintains the virtues of tolerance and peace and a genuine inner civilization. As such, China far surpasses the corrupt and deceitful West. China, fortunately unaffected by European thought, is a country of sages and wise men. We offer our respects to China and the Chinese people. Only in China can we recognize the true path of life. Only in China can we be close to truth and reality. Only in China can we receive the noble discipline of Buddhist monks. The phenomena of turmoil, disharmonious psychology, senseless competition, and blind exploration are unavoidable in today's China. However, beneath this phenomenon, there is still much wisdom and knowledge, and true love can be found in the ancient land of China. O China, the repository and preserver of ancient civilization, we offer our respects to you. Today, Christianized West is gradually collapsing under its evil and foolish policies. A revolutionary China may be able to save this devastated world, not relying on military force, not relying on money, not relying on oil, cotton, rubber, etc., but relying on its goodness, truth, justice, fairness, and its true unity of purpose. O China, the compassionate protector of a world of sinful deceit, we come to China not to teach China foolish doctrines but to learn wisdom from China. We hope and believe that our arrival will bring great benefits. We will dedicate ourselves to moral and spiritual innovation, which is what the world lacks and needs most.

(Denouncing the League of Nations) Within the Jue Lu of Da Xi Road, we now have people from seven countries who, under China's peaceful and tolerant culture, live together as one family, speaking with one voice. We can achieve such merit. Europe has no place to accommodate us, but China welcomes us with open arms. Furthermore, the kindness shown to us by the Chinese people is worthy of our praise. Inner civilization and nobility of thought are lacking in Christian nations but still exist in China. We are willing to be China's loyal and sincere friends. When the need arises, we are willing to offer our services. We wish China peace, prosperity, and tranquil happiness. However, we must say that China must shift its gaze from admiring the West and focus on its own greatness. Those who sow evil will reap its consequences. The way to save an individual and save a nation is not to rely on others, even if they are famous. In reality, they are empty, false, and deceitful, like the "League of Nations." Therefore, to seek salvation, one must rely on one's own knowledge, one's own strength, and one's own struggle. Regarding this point, I may have more to contribute. May China and the Chinese people be happy. May all sentient beings be happy.

Therefore, it was imperative to take my daughter Huayin back to educate her. I said that if the lawyer did not let my daughter go home, I would rather die at the lawyer's place. Subsequently, neighbors, filled with indignation, came to prevent the lawyer's illegal actions, and I was finally able to bring my daughter home. Lawyer Li Chunsen is a lawyer. How could he dare to use an underage girl to incite her to analyze the estate? ㈡ How dare he hide my daughter in his residence upstairs? ㈢ How dare he force me to sign an acknowledgment that my daughter was marrying Shen Tongjia? ㈣ How dare he prevent me from taking my daughter back? Municipal Bureau of Public Works Invents Cold Solvent Oil to Improve Road Construction 129

The Municipal Bureau of Public Works has been actively researching and improving road surfaces in recent years. Previously, it was concerned about the winter cracking and summer melting of asphalt roads. Now, after multiple improvements, it has invented a cold solvent oil that can avoid the above-mentioned drawbacks. Xue Cixin, the head of the Bureau's Third Section, gave a detailed presentation at the National Economic Commission in Nanjing Tietangchi at 5:00 pm on the fourth, at the invitation of the Commission. The details are recorded below:

) Improvement of Coal Ash Roads (Shanghai's roads are generally divided into three types: ㈠ Coal ash roads: after the completion of this type of road surface, it is exceptionally flat and comfortable for the first two or three weeks, but after a few months, it becomes uneven after rain. Vehicles sink deeply when passing over it, and on sunny days, dust obscures the sky. The Bureau has been researching improvements. Initially, a crushed brick base was added to avoid sinking after rain, and the result was very good. However, the dust on sunny days could not be reduced. Later, salt brine was added to the road surface, but it broke easily after heavy vehicles passed over it. Therefore, a satisfactory solution has not been found to date.

(Remediation of Brick and Stone Roads) ㈡ Brick and stone roads: The cost of materials and maintenance for this type of surface is very low. However, due to poor construction techniques, there is often mud after rain. Subsequent attempts to remedy this also used a crushed stone base to reduce unevenness, and the arch of the road was rebuilt using rectangular stones three inches wide and six inches long to make the road flat and solid. To reduce mud, the stone seams were initially filled with cement slurry, but this easily cracked. Later, a powder of asphalt was used to fill the seams, which was effective, but the cost was very high. Therefore, a good solution has not been found. The construction project has been changed from a contracting system to a long-term employee system to reduce the drawbacks of being careless.

(Invention of Cold Solvent Oil) ㈢ Crushed stone roads: The maintenance cost of this road is very high. The surface is covered with asphalt. However, it is prone to cracking in the cold winter. Later, adding asphalt was improved, but although the cracking in winter was reduced, it was easy to dissolve in the hot summer. Now, after hiring British engineering experts to conduct research, a cold solvent oil has been invented. It is a semi-solid made of asphalt and light kerosene. When building, stone chips are added and mixed with a machine, then poured on the road. Vehicles can travel on it immediately. In winter, there is no risk of cracking, and in summer, there is no worry about melting. It can be said that a great success has been achieved.

City Detective Team Cracks Down on Two Gambling Dens in Zhabei 130

| More Than Twenty Gamblers Detained | At 16 Gongxing Lane, Xinmin Road, Datong Road, Zhabei, a hoodlum from Wuxi, Dong A'gen (28 years old), colluded with Li Rongsheng, Shen Xiaoping, and other unemployed vagrants from Shaoxing to secretly establish a gambling den. Prison Warden Accuses Foreman Warden of Obstructing Official Duty 132

Wu Bingyan, a candidate warden from E Province serving in the Second Special District Prison of the French Concession, during an inspection of all prison cells around 1 PM on the 25th of last month, found Gong Bin, a foreman warden and fellow townsman, removing his uniform hat and unbuttoning his collar while on duty in the exercise yard. Wu reprimanded him for improper etiquette, to which Gong replied that it was hot and he was wiping sweat. Wu then reported this to Warden Sun Xiong. Gong rushed to the public office to argue with Wu, and a conflict ensued. Wu allegedly threw an inkstone from the desk, hitting Gong's head and causing bleeding. Colleagues separated them, and Gong reported Wu to the Central Police Station for assault and battery. The police chief sent detectives to the prison to arrest Wu, who was transferred to the Second Special District Court the following day, and prosecuted for assault. Details of the interrogation were reported in a previous issue. Subsequently, after further hearings, the court ruled that the plaintiff, Gong Hanbin, had not presented sufficient evidence, and acquitted the defendant, Wu Bingyan. Gong, dissatisfied with the verdict, requested the police department to appeal, alleging obstruction of official duty and requesting an investigation and punishment. The prosecutor, Wang Ren, accompanied by clerk Zhao Fen, opened an investigation hearing in the Fifth Tribunal the day before yesterday, summoning the plaintiff Wu Bingyan and three warden witnesses to the court for questioning. Electrician Electrocuted 134

According to Guomin News Agency, Wang Buxian is the principal of Yuqun Middle School, a private school in Jiangwan. The school employed an electrician named Jiang Akang, 23 years old, from Wuxi. At around 6 PM the night before last, the school's flagpole light was damaged. Jiang went up to repair it. Huang Fuyuan Commits Suicide Due to Inability to Make a Living 135

Huang Fuyuan, a carpenter from Dengyanghang, Gaoqiao, Pudong, was 34 years old. Huang was lazy and often stopped working, making it difficult to support himself. Five years ago, his wife, unable to endure hunger and cold, ran away with her lover. After his wife left, Huang did not improve, continuing his idle ways. Unable to find consistent work or even a full meal, he relied on his brother, Huang Linyuan, for sustenance. Eventually, he felt ashamed and resentful of the criticism, so he bought two bottles of sleeping medication and consumed them in his room the night before last. The next day, his brother, wondering why Huang Fuyuan had not risen, entered the room and found him dead. Shocked, he reported to the Third District, Fourth Station, which dispatched police to the scene. Two empty medicine bottles were found, confirming suicide. The police instructed the local headman to report the death to the local court for investigation. Prosecutor Zhang and others arrived at the scene to examine the body and ordered it to be prepared for burial, pending further investigation.

Xu Duckling Granted Probation for Theft 136

Chen Amao, a rickshaw puller from Yangzhou residing at No. 1199, Wuzhou Road, and his wife Xu Duckling, 36 years old, separated in November 1931. Chen Amao had moved his mistress, Fan Lishi, into their home, and Xu Duckling became jealous. Their relationship deteriorated, and the couple quarreled often before Duckling disappeared. Chen Amao hired lawyer Huang Xiubo to file two lawsuits in the First Special District Court: one accusing her of absconding with property and the other seeking a divorce. Xu Duckling failed to appear at the initial hearings for both cases. At 9 AM on May 7 of last year, Xu Duckling, along with several others, broke into Chen Amao's home while he was away and made off with two trunks of clothing and a foreign stove, worth 100 yuan. Chen returned home and, discovering the missing items, reported the theft to the police, accusing Xu Duckling and her accomplices of robbery and requesting their arrest. Over a year later, on July 21 of this year, Chinese and Western detectives from the Yangshupu Police Station apprehended Xu Duckling in the Chinese area along with a suspect, Wang Tianbao, also from Yangzhou. After investigation, it was determined that Wang (her lover) was not involved in the theft, and he was released. Xu Duckling admitted to taking the trunks, claiming they were her own possessions and that she had been driven away by Chen Amao and his mistress, Fan Lishi. She denied running away and claimed to be unaware of the divorce proceedings. Lawyer Huang Xiubo was summoned, but he could not prove the divorce. The court ordered a postponement for further investigation. The day before yesterday, Judge Xiao Xiefen continued the hearing in the Third Criminal Court, stating that Chen Amao's divorce suit against Xu Duckling was a default judgment served by public notice. He questioned both plaintiffs and defendants at length, and their testimonies remained as before. Lawyer Jiang Heli represented Xu Duckling and requested leniency, arguing that she was a woman who did not read newspapers and was unaware of the public notice of divorce. The court sentenced Xu Duckling to one year of imprisonment, suspended for three years, for the crime of "theft by three or more persons."

Elderly Woman Hangs Herself, Lover Flees 142

An elderly woman named Chen Dai, from Yancheng, over 40 years old, lived with her lover, Lu Jincheng, in a thatched shed at a certain address in Yuque Port, Rihui Bridge, Nanshi. Their relationship was very close and they acted like husband and wife. Chen Dai had a son from a previous marriage, Chen Chaoju, who was in his early twenties and raised by Lu Jincheng. Last night, Chen and Lu had an argument over household matters. Lu went out to cool off. When he returned home around 3 AM the next morning, he saw Chen had hanged herself in the living room. There were obvious red marks on her neck, but no rope was visible. He quickly took her down and fled. Neighbors discovered the body around 6 AM and reported it to the Second District Public Security Bureau, which then instructed the local headman to report it to the court for examination. Hongqiao Town Merchants Petition the Municipal Government to Dredge the River 145

After the Shanghai West Puhui Tang River was contracted out in sections for dredging by the Public Works Bureau, the first two sections have been completed after more than four months. However, the fourth and fifth sections from Hongqiao Town to Jiepai Bridge were contracted to Shen Rongji. Due to prolonged work stoppages, the depth and width of the channel differ greatly from the original dimensions. As the deadline set by the Public Works Bureau is approaching, the contractor has reduced the amount of earth removed and piled the silt from the riverbed onto the banks. This will inevitably wash back into the river during rains. Furthermore, the contractor has reportedly submitted a request to superiors for acceptance and inspection. Consequently, shops throughout Hongqiao Town are opposing this. They have requested Pan Boxian, a member of the town's river dredging committee, to petition the Municipal Government to order the Public Works Bureau to demolish all the sheds built along the banks, rebuild the river to the defined width of six zhang, and re-dredge the river. Meanwhile, more than 40 shops, including Yilong, Yuanlong, Tongchang, Yimao, Fuji, Zhongdetang, Santai, Yichang, and Chengji, have jointly petitioned the Public Works Bureau to order the contractor, Shen Rongji, to dredge the river in accordance with the defined depth, width, and dimensions, and not to reduce the amount of earth removed, in order to benefit navigation and complete the project.

No Genuine Cholera Found on the Beijing-Shanghai Line 146

The Railway Bureau requested the capital to temporarily suspend inspections. The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau received a report from the Capital Summer Epidemic Prevention Joint Office that genuine cholera had been discovered in Suzhou and planned to send personnel to inspect passengers arriving at the Beijing-Shanghai train stations to prevent the spread. The bureau immediately instructed the health department to discuss and respond. The report stated that the Central Cholera Bureau held a meeting in Shanghai, which the department chief also attended. At the meeting, the committee members carefully examined reports from various locations. From Shanghai to Suzhou and Nanjing, no genuine cholera was discovered. The bureau reported that the report from Suzhou claimed to have discovered genuine cholera. However, this report was also submitted for review at the Central Cholera Bureau meeting and was deemed insufficient to confirm the discovery of genuine cholera. Furthermore, more than a thousand passengers travel by small boat and private ship from Suzhou to Nanjing every week. If the waterways are not inspected, inspecting only train stations will inconvenience passengers traveling north to Beijing and Shanghai. Based on the above reasons, the bureau should request the Capital Summer Epidemic Prevention Joint Office to temporarily suspend inspections at Xiaguan Station. When genuine cholera is confirmed, the bureau will send a doctor to assist in the process. The bureau believed that these facts were accurate and formally replied to the Capital Summer Epidemic Prevention Joint Office to request a temporary suspension of the inspections.

French Consulate General Announces Amendments to Traffic Regulations 147

The French Consulate General in Shanghai issued Order No. 163, stating, "For the purpose of enforcing regulations, the resolution of the Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council meeting held on July 10, 1933, is hereby approved. In accordance with Article 13 of the Organization Charter of the Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council, promulgated by this Consulate General's Order of January 15, 1927, the following amendments to Articles 17 and 38 of the Traffic Regulations of the Shanghai French Concession Municipal Council are hereby promulgated:

'Article 17' Special provisions for various locations on public roads (traffic on Rue du Consulat, Avenue Kédong, Avenue Édouard VII, and one-way traffic on certain roads). On Avenue Édouard VII, no vehicle shall overtake other vehicles traveling in the same direction, but all vehicles may overtake trucks and buses. On Avenue Kédong (the section from Baixianqiao Small Vegetable Market to Avenue de Messimy) and Rue du Consulat (to Quai de France), slow-moving vehicles and vehicles with a speed less than 30 kilometers per hour may only be overtaken by drivers in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of these regulations. However, the driver shall be fully responsible for any accidents caused by overtaking, even if the fault lies with others. Trucks and buses are not allowed to overtake other vehicles on Rue du Consulat and Avenue Kédong (the section from Baixianqiao Small Vegetable Market to Quai de France). On the following roads, as well as other roads to be subsequently specified, vehicles shall only travel in the designated one-way direction from 8 AM to 6 PM. On Rue du Père Froc, vehicles shall travel from Rue Hua Long towards Avenue Massenet. On Rue Che Pa-san, vehicles shall travel from Rue du Consulat towards Avenue Édouard VII.

'Article 38' Signals. Drivers of vehicles, persons leading livestock, and pedestrians shall stop when facing a red light indicating that the road is closed. They may proceed when facing a green light indicating that the road is open."

On Eyes 153

— Nineteen

From the lines "The eye has the same view of colors, and one view is the same" and "Heaven sees as the people see, and seeing is one," we can deduce that heaven gave people a pair of eyes in order to unify their vision. However, due to the changes in color and the complexity of events, like treacherous waves and unpredictable clouds, it is impossible to grasp; as a result, people see things differently according to their own perspectives and wisdom. Although this can be said to be the art of the eye, it has lost the original intention of heaven giving people eyes.

For example, "Xi Shi" must come from the eyes of a "lover." It seems that if one is not a "lover," "Xi Shi" will not appear in their eyes. When dominoes click, the eyes will feel cool. Now that the West is gradually influencing China, it is said that foreigners have also started playing mahjong. This shows that dominoes do have the effect of cooling the eyes. The above two examples are about the amazing things about the eyes, which everyone knows. People see things differently according to their own perspectives and wisdom. In other words, everyone's views are different. "Play mahjong, national affairs, screw them." This is also a point of view. If 400 million compatriots could all see it this way, the nation's vision could be unified. "Internal pacification and external resistance" once caused a great uproar. This is also because the views of the upper and lower levels are different. Furthermore, adversity can build a nation. However, the words "national crisis" are now rarely seen even in the newspapers. Presumably, weapons of war have been transformed into jade and silk, and the world can be peaceful from now on. This is another difference in viewpoints. Jiao Da in the Dream of the Red Chamber saw that the pair of stone lions in front of the Jia Mansion were clean. Regardless of whether the view is correct or not, it is not easy for a rude man to see the small details.

In short, the eye is indeed a very mysterious thing. It is impossible for heaven to unify the vision of ordinary people. "Heaven sees" is the same as "the people see." The "people see" are so different, I wonder what the "heaven sees" is like. How can we call out to heaven and ask?

Automobiles Rampant in the Interior 154

— A Stiffened Chrysalis

"The road is like a tiger; one must not walk in the middle of it." In bustling cities, cars roar, galloping around like fierce tigers. One moment of carelessness, and the blood of the common people, crushed by the car's wheels, immediately splatters, painting the road a dazzling red. Cars are a necessity for the wealthy to get around—fast, stable, and authentically foreign. As a result, officials, scholars, compradors, the rich, fashionable women, and modern young masters abound. Such figures must ride in a car to demonstrate their nobility. Just look at Nanjing Road, from morning till night, endlessly winding like two celestial poisonous dragons, and you can see how alarmingly popular cars have become.

Shanghai is, after all, the Paris of the East. Although the blood of commoners splatters on the roads on average several times a day, the rich can resolve everything by simply pulling out their wallets. After all, commoners are an overabundant commodity in Shanghai. The more commoners' blood is shed, the higher the value of the rich becomes, and the more civilized the metropolis appears.

Cars are indeed the most urgently needed tool for transportation. As a result, everywhere in the interior feels the need. Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Hangzhou...one place after another has discovered this most modern and stable mode of transportation, galloping swiftly and reliably on several expanded roads.

Although Suzhou is a cultural land with the quintessential characteristics of antiquity, after the expansion of Guanqian Street, Hulong Street, and Jingde Road, it already possesses the rudimentary form of Shanghai's roads. The newly emerging ancient city requires cars as the most modern embellishment. Consequently, a group of Suzhou celebrities jointly submitted a petition to the county government, requesting permission to allow cars to operate in order to revitalize the market, facilitate transportation, and aid commerce. How important! This modern request. Especially during this sweltering season for cruising around.

The blood of commoners, crushed by cars, paints the road with color, and the people of the interior can also broaden their horizons.

Beware!

From Watermelon Season to Rural Economic Panic 156

— Yu Youqing

Watermelon is originally a summer refreshment. The ancients said it well... "Floating watermelon and sinking plums." In the past, watermelons were indeed a summer drink, but they have been degenerating year after year. Because in the city, there are many other things to relieve the heat, such as ice cream, sour plum juice, and tangerine and fruit syrups. Why must one eat watermelon? As a result, watermelon has become a refreshing fruit for middle and lower-class families.

This year's watermelons in the Suzhou area are at most only about two yuan, and in the past few days, the price has dropped a lot, only costing a little over one yuan per dan (a unit of weight). How much profit can the villagers make from a watermelon costing a little over one yuan per dan? And sometimes, they can't even sell them, still arriving full of boats and returning full of boats. If rural by-products cannot be sold smoothly, then a rural economic panic will surely occur. Therefore, seeing watermelons come to market makes me feel the rural economic panic. This is a fact placed before us, and there is no denying it.

From the fact that watermelons cannot be sold smoothly, we can talk about the inability of national silk to develop. Because ice cream and tangerine juice are like wool and serge transported from Europe and America, while watermelon is like domestically produced silk. In other words, silk cannot be developed, just as watermelon cannot be sold smoothly. We must defeat ice cream and tangerine juice so that watermelons can be sold smoothly and so that the rural economy is not completely hopeless, with a glimmer of dawn. We should love and use domestically produced silk and love to eat watermelon to save some of the rural economy from bankruptcy. Otherwise, China's countryside will truly decline.

People who love to eat ice cream and tangerine juice, eat more watermelons.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 157

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twelve. The poor and lowly suffer hardship when they join the army; a sick man falls behind and sacrifices himself; willingly doffing his uniform, the amorous warrior Zhao Ziqiang takes off his military hat with his left hand and strokes his head several times with his right, smiling, "That's a long story." Saying this, he takes out his pocket watch and glances at it, already without time to allow him to speak further, and stands up, saying, "Let's talk next time I come back." Miss Jiang thinks to herself, this company commander, for no reason, ran over to sit for a while, only saying he wants to change his profession. Whether you change your profession or not, what are you telling us for? Could it be that he knows what I mean, unwilling to have a soldier as a son-in-law, so he wants to change his profession? That would be really something! Thinking this, she also smiles. Zhao Ziqiang thinks, as soon as he says he wants to change his profession, his future wife smiles, and his future mother-in-law also smiles. Looking at it this way, the profession truly cannot but be changed. With such a dumb riddle in his stomach, he walks with his head lowered, all the way thinking about returning to the camp. Walking on the road, hearing the bugle sound, seeing the white buildings of Xiyuan, and even the gray uniform on his body, he feels that nothing is not old-fashioned to the point of annoyance. If he doesn't change his profession and gets married, one person will be at home, and the other will be in the camp. Not to mention that it would be wasting his wife's youth, why did he marry a wife in the first place? If he changes his profession, no matter what he does, the two of them can always be together. No wonder some girls don't want to marry soldiers; marrying a person is just an empty name, truly being a "grass widow"! The more he thinks, the more he agrees, and he must change his profession! Now is not some urgent time, so resigning his post should be possible. For the sake of love, he will sacrifice this company commander position and resign tomorrow. Thinking this, he returns to the company headquarters, no longer having any hesitation, and wants to approach that sergeant to discuss how to request his resignation. As for what he usually thinks about, such as resisting Japan and serving the country, he has not a bit of it in his mind. Here, we can see how he goes to find his new life. (151)

Inside the Detention Center 158

— Tiger Head

The source of the facts is as follows... I have a friend who was detained in a detention center for two days and nights on suspicion of murder. Based on what he told me about fragments of news from inside the detention center, I am now recording these words below, which can also be considered a timely article under Mr. Dong Shoujing's plea for prisoners. (The following are my friend's words)

The police accidentally killed the old quartermaster in my shop while cleaning their guns. At the time, I planned to have the police pay some money as funeral expenses for the old quartermaster; and I would also add some compensation as relief funds for the bereaved family. It seemed like it could pass peacefully? Who knew that at this time, someone would come out using bamboo-splitting methods to make me spend more money? Tell me, who would want to do that? The reason I was willing to spend some money on relief was because he was an old member of the shop, and it was unfortunate that the quartermaster died, so compensating some money was to comfort the heart and did not mean I had to take on any responsibility. I frankly refused. They then framed me with "trumped-up" charges and put me in jail. This was two weeks ago. The place I was detained in was Detention Center No. 14. It was only a small room about five feet wide and less than two zhang (approximately 20 feet) long. Above the room was a small hole like a ventilation window, fitted with iron bars. The hole was for the prisoners to breathe, and the iron bars were to prevent jailbreaks. Inside the small room, there were already fifteen or sixteen people, with long gowns, short jackets, all kinds of people. The exit was only a small door that could barely be passed by sideways. A wooden bucket was placed in the corner inside the door, where people urinated and defecated. Now that it's summer, the room is small and crowded, and the stench is overwhelming and unbearable! But these people have been here for many days and are just like "being in a shop selling abalone, and not smelling the stench after a long time." They seemed to be at ease! These fifteen or sixteen people, distinguished by the types of crimes they committed, were indeed diverse and interesting to see! Communists, opium addicts, red pill users, flower society members, adulterers, drunkards and fighters... all kinds of people; someone like me, suspected of murder, was probably the only one! Among them, the most common were those who committed adultery. No wonder stories of rape and seduction can often be found in social news. Shanghai is truly a world of lust! This detention center also provided food every day. The daytime was almost evenly divided to provide two meals, so when eating, I felt there was a big difference compared to normal times. This kind of food, if you called it rice, had a lot of water, and you could hardly tell it was rice. If you called it porridge, you couldn't see your face reflected in the many waters, so it didn't seem like you could call it porridge. As for the color of the rice... it was neither black nor white, roughly between black and white, and it was very unpleasant to look at. The vegetable was a light cabbage soup. How could anyone swallow it? Fortunately, I was only detained for two days and nights and was able to endure the hunger and not eat it. If it had been extended for a few more days, I would have had to learn from Mr. Gandhi and go on a hunger strike. Opium, cigarettes, and matches were also supplied here. These were originally things that prisoners did not need, so they were priced very high. Each opium bubble cost at least two big yuan. I didn't see any whole cigarettes. The so-called cigarette butts that one wouldn't normally smoke cost thirty copper coins each. Each match cost fifty wen. Therefore, smoking a cigarette butt cost 350 wen, and if you were unlucky enough to be detected by the inspectors, you would also be subjected to increased punishment. For example, when A and B were smoking a cigarette butt together, when A smoked, B would fan it, and when B smoked, A would fan it. This fanning was not because it was hot in the summer, but to fan out the smell of the cigarette to avoid being punished again. Opium bubbles were the most difficult to pass around. It is said that entrusting the food deliveryman was the most reliable, because when the food deliveryman delivered the food, the prison door was open, and he had to hide it in the bottom of the bowl and secretly transport it. Although the plan was meticulous, it was also extremely painstaking. Pancakes and fried dough sticks were originally the food that poor friends used to fill their stomachs, so their price was the same as outside. Eating vegetables seemed to have a bit of an aristocratic color, so the fees were higher. It was still a fair arrangement?

My friend was talking to this point when someone called him to answer the phone, so the conversation was interrupted.

Education News

Important News: Results of the Guangdong Provincial Middle School Joint Entrance Examination 159

The joint examination was held simultaneously in sixty-four counties and cities. A total of nine thousand four hundred and eighty-three candidates took the examination, and approximately eight thousand eight hundred and eighty-five passed. The test papers for the Guangdong Provincial Middle School Graduation Joint Entrance Examination, provincial and municipal joint examinations have been reviewed one after another. For the provincial joint examination, excluding the two sections of provincial and municipal middle schools in the Guangzhou area, there were sixty-four counties and cities participating in the joint examination simultaneously. The total number of candidates was nine thousand four hundred and eighty-three, including eight hundred and sixty-one in the senior high school general program, five hundred and sixty-two in the senior high school normal program, and eight thousand and sixty-one in the junior high school program. Because this was the first graduation joint entrance examination, the authorities, considering the local circumstances, made the test questions not too difficult. Students who usually studied diligently had no risk of failing. Therefore, in the results of the examination, among the nine thousand four hundred and eighty-three candidates, approximately eight thousand eight hundred and eighty-five passed, including six hundred and ninety-seven in the senior high school general program, five hundred and eleven in the senior high school normal program, and six thousand six hundred and seventy-seven in the junior high school program. Now, in order to facilitate the promotion of joint entrance examination passers to higher education, the Provincial Department of Education has specially published a booklet of joint entrance examination results, comprising five volumes. In it, the passing students, supplementary examination candidates, and students held back a grade are listed one by one and sent to the various levels of schools that are recruiting new students this year for reference. If passing students apply to take promotion examinations, the booklet of results will be used as proof. The joint entrance examination graduation certificates will be verified and issued later. As for the students in each middle school throughout the province who failed the graduation joint entrance examination, a supplementary examination will be held on the 18th of this month at the Jiaozhong School in Guangzhou City. The Guangzhou Municipal Middle School Graduation Joint Entrance Examination was also held simultaneously with the provincial middle school graduation joint entrance examination on July 10th and 11th. The test papers have now been reviewed. According to the results, the municipal middle school students participating in the joint examination included one hundred and one in the senior high school normal program. One hundred passed all subjects, and one failed one subject. Forty-five students took the senior high school general program joint examination. Forty-three passed all subjects, one failed one subject, and one failed three subjects. Thirty-one students took the senior high school science program joint examination, and one failed three subjects. Ninety-nine students took the examination from the First Middle School. Ninety-three passed all subjects, five failed one subject, and one failed two subjects. One hundred and seventy-two students took the examination from the First Middle School. One hundred and forty passed all subjects, seventeen failed one subject, ten failed two subjects, four failed three subjects, and one failed five subjects. One hundred and three students took the examination from the Second Middle School. Seventy-one passed all subjects, twenty-three failed one subject, five failed two subjects, and four failed three subjects. Sixty-nine students took the examination from the Third Middle School. Fifty-four passed all subjects, eleven failed one subject, and four failed two subjects. Those who passed are approved to graduate. Those who failed one or two subjects must take a supplementary examination. Those who failed three or more subjects are ordered to repeat a grade. It is also scheduled to hold the municipal middle school graduation joint entrance examination supplementary examination on the 4th and 5th of this month at the Municipal Normal School.

Various Sectors to Visit Educational Institutions 166

The Municipal Bureau of Education Formulates Reception Methods. The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education announced that in order to facilitate educational researchers or groups to visit educational institutions in the city, seven articles of the reception methods for visitors to educational institutions in the city have been formulated and will be implemented immediately. All municipal and registered private schools and social educational institutions in the city must follow these reception methods. The methods are copied below and circulated for your information. The attached reception methods for visitors to educational institutions in the city are as follows: 1. Those who wish to visit educational institutions in the city must first contact the bureau to arrange reception. 2. The reception methods for visitors by this bureau are divided into the following three types: A. Issuing an introduction certificate, and assigning staff to guide when necessary. B. Answering questions about education in the city. C. Providing complimentary publications of this bureau at its discretion. 3. Visits are not allowed on holidays and when visits would interfere with work, or the visit time will be rescheduled. 4. The reception of visitors by the educational institutions in the city should be based on the introduction certificate from this bureau. 5. For those who visit educational institutions in the city for special missions, the reception methods will be determined on a case-by-case basis. 6. These methods may be revised at any time. 7. These methods will be implemented from the date of announcement.

Kun Fan Girls' Junior Middle School, located at Qingdao Intersection on Mei Baige Road, has been striving for perfection since moving to its new location. The student body has increased dramatically from over one hundred to over five hundred students. Other equipment such as books, physics, chemistry, and machinery have also been purchased and completed successively. Starting next semester, the school will emphasize hands-on learning in all subjects, striving to thoroughly implement the purpose of education for production. It is heard that the number of new student applications is extremely high, and the existing classrooms are difficult to accommodate. Therefore, the adjacent houses have been rented and renovated to expand the facilities. As for the teachers at all levels, experienced and scholarly physical education graduates have already been hired.

French Vietnam Requests to Participate in Next Year's Far Eastern Games 176

A formal letter has been submitted to the Philippine Sports Association, which still requires the full agreement of China and Japan. (Manila Correspondence) The Tenth Far Eastern Games will be held here in the early summer of next year. French Vietnam has recently formally submitted a letter to the Far Eastern Amateur Athletic Association requesting to join the Far Eastern Games as a member. The Philippine Amateur Athletic Association has received the official request from Vietnam, but according to the Far Eastern Games Charter passed in Tokyo in 1930, this request must be unanimously agreed upon by China and Japan. A new country wishing to participate in the Games must first have the unanimous approval of China, Japan, and the Philippines.

Sending Twenty Athletes 177

According to officials of the Vietnam Amateur Athletic Association when sending the request, Vietnam has at least twenty athletes who can be sent to the Far Eastern Games in Manila next year. Recently, the French Consulate in the Philippines inquired with the Philippine Amateur Association about the amount of subsidies from the Philippine government for next year's Games, which will be used as the standard for the French government's subsidy for Vietnamese athletes.

Radio Broadcasting of the Charter 178

The Vietnam Amateur Athletic Association requested to become a member of the Far Eastern Games and stated its full compliance with and agreement to the Far Eastern Games Charter and Article 12 regarding amateur qualifications. This article on amateur qualifications for the Far Eastern Games has been translated into French and broadcast via radio throughout Vietnam.

Next Year's Far Eastern Games 179

In the letter requesting participation in the Games, Vietnam also inquired about the confirmed date of next year's Games. After deliberation at a meeting of the Far Eastern Games Committee of the Philippine Sports Association on July 28, it was officially postponed to June 9 to 17, for a total of eight days.

Shanghai-Kunming Long-Distance Running Practice Race Held Yesterday 184

The Shanghai-Kunming long-distance running event organized by the Chinese Sports Association held a practice run yesterday morning, using the Shanghai-Songhu section as the basis. The start was originally scheduled for 4:30 AM, but due to incomplete team members, it was delayed until 5:00 AM. Starting from the Songhu Railway Station on Baoshan Road, heading north, passing the Commercial Press to Tiantong Nunnery, entering Jiangwan Road, turning into the West Sports Association Road, crossing the racecourse to Jiangwan Station, following the railway to Zhanghuabang Station, then turning into Jungong Road, crossing Wuncaobang Bridge, returning to the railway, along Wusong Town to Paotaiwan, a total distance of 11 and 3/4 miles. Li Yagu, a member of the Baihong team, guided everything along the way. At the beginning, Zheng Renan took the lead, followed by Sun Qixing, with Gong Bangfu and Zhu Yunfu competing for third and fourth place. At Wuncaobang, Zhu took third place, and Gong gradually fell behind. The final results were: 1st Zheng Renan, 2nd Sun Qixing, 3rd Zhu Xuefu, 4th Gong Bangfu, reaching the finish line in 1 hour, 18 minutes, and 50 seconds. If there are no problems, the association's Shanghai-Kunming long-distance race will be held on the 20th of this month, and non-members are welcome to participate. You can register with Huang Shengbai at Meixi Elementary School on Penglai Road.

Special Publication

National Defense Education (1) 198

Professor Zhang Qiyun of Central University Speaks on Tzu Tao's Notes. Professor Zhang Qiyun of Central University is an expert in Chinese geography and history, and his various history and geography books are popular. Currently, Mr. Zhang is also a member of the Central National Defense Commission and has thoroughly researched national defense education. The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, recognizing that national defense is the foundation of a country and that national defense education is particularly urgent, invited Mr. Zhang to give a special lecture at the summer school of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education. At first, Mr. Zhang declined repeatedly due to his work on the National Defense Commission, but after repeated letters of invitation from Hu Changcai, the section chief of the Bureau of Education, he finally agreed to come to Shanghai and give four lectures a day. The topics and content of his lectures are recorded separately below.

First Lecture: Discussing National Defense Education from the Perspective of National Defense Concepts 199

Since the Sino-Japanese War of 1894-95 and the Boxer Rebellion, China has faced severe national crises and deep pain. People of insight have gradually begun to promote military-national education through speech and writing. Among the representative figures is Mr. Jiang Baili. Mr. Jiang proposed three methods for the military and schools to cooperate: (1) Elementary schools should practice small team drills. (2) Middle schools and normal schools should practice medium-sized team training. (3) Higher schools and higher normal schools should practice large team training. Higher education should pay particular attention to military systems, strategies, and key national defense tasks. In terms of spiritual training, Mr. Jiang advocated diligence, hardship, and strength to cultivate the nation's foundation, and to inspire the nation's spirit with literature and art. Therefore, when Chinese people ask about national defense education,

Mr. Jiang should be regarded as the most outstanding.

In the first year of the Republic of China, the purpose of education was announced: "Focus on moral education, supplemented by practical education and military-national education, and complete it with aesthetic education." However, if we look back at the atmosphere of the early Republic of China, the so-called military-national education was nothing more than a formality and had little practical effect. This is something we have all experienced. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, an educational survey was held in Beijing, with Fan Yuanlian, Cai Yuanpei, Wang Chonghui, Wu Jingheng, and others participating. At this time, the European War had ended, and the world was advocating peace. The educational survey proposed to abolish militarist democracy and replace it with "cultivating sound personality and developing national spirit" as the purpose. This proposal was adopted and promulgated by the Ministry of Education. We do not wish to criticize the views of these gentlemen. National character should be based on sound personality, and national defense should be based on national spirit. Theoretically, there is nothing wrong with this, but in reality, it is still too abstract and lacks specific and effective measures.

After the establishment of the National Government, the Three Principles of the People were clearly defined as the purpose of moral education. Originally, the Prime Minister's teachings contained profound national defense considerations in every aspect. However, there are not many people who can develop the Prime Minister's legacy. To be honest, in recent years, it has been like "buying a casket and returning the pearl." The Prime Minister's industrial plan is like the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan, and at its core is a national defense plan. Its purpose is to mechanize the military. Unfortunately, in recent years, this legacy has often been shelved and few people have asked about it. Looking at the first part of the industrial plan, the Prime Minister tells us to designate Duolun as the main base for immigration policy, to station more than one million demobilized troops near Duolun, to build a double-track railway from Duolun to the northern major port, and to invite military experts to guide the immigration movement. There are also many very detailed and thoughtful plans. Not to mention that people in the government almost ignored the Duolun policy, how many people in schools are willing to pay attention to and study it? Recently, the word Duolun has been making headlines in newspapers, but it is already too late to mend the fold after the sheep are lost.

The Chinese people's biggest problem is that they steal empty names to amuse themselves. They learn a few slogans and think they have fulfilled their responsibility. So, whether it is military-national education, moral education, personality education, Three Principles of the People education, or the newest national defense education, the cyclical replacement of these terms cannot save China. We need careful theories, detailed articles, not only practical plans, but also serious implementation. Having said that, ordinary people still have a superficial understanding of the word "national defense" and do not understand the whole picture. They ultimately believe that national defense is the military, and the military is raising soldiers. Putting on a military uniform and carrying a gun makes one a military national. That is truly losing the mark by a mile. Our country raises the most soldiers, accounting for the first place in the world. According to recent statistics, the combined standing armies of the five powerful countries of Britain, the United States, France, Russia, and Japan are only 1.5 million people. China has 1.8 million standing troops and 700,000 miscellaneous troops, totaling 2.5 million people. If that is the case, wouldn't China be

the strongest country in the world?

I once gave a speech intended to correct the common misconception of national defense, roughly meaning that national defense (1) is not the military's national defense, but the people's national defense; (2) is not a national defense for dying, but a national defense for maintaining life; (3) is not a defensive national defense, but an offensive national defense; (4) not only focuses on tangible national defense, but also pays attention to intangible national defense. The Chinese army is called the National Revolutionary Army. The meaning of the National Army is the people's army, that is, the new national defense should take the entire people as the source. In theory, the focus of China's national defense is not on a small number of frontline soldiers, but on the entire national army, and even more so on the entire population. The entire Chinese territory should be like a standing military camp, and the entire population should be like a standing military force. The right to protect China should be shared by all the people. The true nature of national defense should be that the entire people are engaged in it. However, in reality, it is greatly disappointing. The people and the military can be said to have no connection, each not interfering with the other, divided into two sectors. The majority of the people, who are connected to the fate of the country, are merely spectators, leaving a small number of people to resolve their fate. The people regard military affairs as the monopoly of the military and do not interfere, and the military also regards military affairs as its monopoly and does not want people to interfere. Alas, with this to face a powerful enemy, how can there not be a great defeat?

Shen Bao Medical Weekly

A Discussion of Jiao Yitang's Letter to the Nation Regarding the Implementation of National Medicine Regulations 200

— Yu Yunxiu

Mr. Jiao is a legislator in our China, and also the head of the National Medicine Hall. Regarding the National Medicine Regulations case at the Central Political Conference on June 7th, he published a letter to the nation, spanning nearly ten thousand words. After reading it, I was truly perplexed. Now, I would like to discuss my doubts with Mr. Jiao and the nation.

Mr. Jiao said, "Since Western medicine was introduced to our China, in order to avoid confusion with Western medicine, the term 'National Medicine' was specifically put forward as the main body. This is similar to how our Chinese writing originally had no need to be called 'National Language,' but because different languages such as English, German, and Japanese were discovered, it became extremely necessary to put forward the term 'National Language' as the main body. The meaning of National Medicine is the same." I find this argument to be illogical. Medicine is a natural science, while writing is an artificial symbol. How can they be compared? When it comes to the origin of writing, there are, of course, bases such as pictographs, ideographs, and phonetic loans. However, later on, ancient scripts evolved into seal scripts, then clerical scripts, and finally the current standard scripts. The current clerical script focuses solely on convenience for daily use, and the principles of pictographs, etc., have been abandoned. I ask, what pictographic basis is there in the current way of writing the characters for "sun" and "moon"? However, ordinary people all know that the sun is the sun and the moon is the moon, and there is no need to explain it using principles of images. Moreover, if the ancient or seal script versions of the characters for "sun" and "moon" are presented, they might be turned upside down and become unrecognizable. This shows that writing is entirely a national custom, an artificial symbol that is forcibly made. I can say that calling heaven "earth" or a deer a "horse" is in no way restricted by truth or reality. However, when discussing medicine, it is absolutely impossible to fabricate things arbitrarily. Yu Lichu's "Classified Drafts" states that Chinese people have seven orifices in their hearts, while Westerners have four, and that Chinese people have two testicles, while Westerners have four. This is ultimately the ravings of a madman. Liu Wansu, Li Dongyuan, Zhu Danxi, and their ilk said that stroke is caused by fire, qi, or phlegm, but it is ultimately a cerebral hemorrhage. As a result, their methods of treating stroke are said to treat fire, qi, or phlegm, but they ultimately do not treat fire, qi, or phlegm. The medicines they use to treat stroke are said to be for treating fire, qi, or phlegm, but they ultimately do not have the effects of treating fire, qi, or phlegm. In short, they are completely inconsistent with truth and reality. In other words, they are completely groundless nonsense. How can this become an academic discipline? Therefore, writing follows custom and can vary from country to country. Medicine is based on truth and has no room for differences. To put it simply, English, German, Japanese, and Chinese can have different languages, but English, German, Japanese, and National medicine cannot be established academically. I ask Mr. Jiao and the nation to distinguish this clearly first. Mr. Jiao said, "Originally, academics have no national boundaries, so there is no so-called National or Western medicine... Only those that are truly beneficial to people in the world should be promoted... People who study medicine should delve into theoretical research." I agree with this wholeheartedly. But I do not know why Mr. Jiao still wants to put forward the term "National Medicine" to avoid confusion with Western medicine. This is the first thing I ask Mr. Jiao to explain. My second request is that Mr. Jiao not forget his own great advocacy of the scholarly attitude of "delving into theoretical research," and I also ask the nation to keep it in mind as a witness.

Mr. Jiao said, "However, domestic medical circles have shown very little academic research, and business competition is becoming increasingly fierce. It is either Western medicine attacking National medicine, or National medicine discrediting Western medicine..." I want to ask Mr. Jiao, which writings of Western medicine attacking National medicine are not academic research, and which are business competition? Which declarations of National medicine discrediting Western medicine are academic research, and which are not business competition? Please examine impartially, weigh the evidence, and make a statistical analysis. I can boldly say that our attacks on National medicine are entirely academic research, while National medicine's discrediting of us is entirely business competition, because National medicine has no academic basis, only business.

Mr. Jiao said, "The state's promotion of medicine and society's support of doctors are like fathers and elder brothers supporting their younger siblings and nannies breastfeeding infants. Their love and care can be said to be meticulous. If doctors do not repay this with academic achievements and instead bicker over the distinction between Chinese and Western factions, how can the state and society place their hopes on domestic medical professionals?" I want to rephrase this and say that the people's expectations of the Legislative Yuan and their support of Mr. Jiao are like younger siblings respecting their fathers and elder brothers and infants yearning for their nannies. Their sincerity of love and respect can be said to be meticulous. If Mr. Jiao does not correct the trend in academic research and instead, as the head of the National Medicine Hall, sophistically argues to compete for dominance, even at the expense of disrupting the education system and seizing administrative power, how can he face the people?

The National Medicine Hall's Desire to Divide Political Power is No Different From Establishing Another Government 201

— Wang Qizhang

Those of us who have read history feel that the feudal lords of the Eastern Zhou Dynasty who revered the royal court and the military commissioners of the prosperous Tang Dynasty who specialized in wielding power were examples of dividing political power and destroying the entire national organization. Recently, at the end of the declining Qing Dynasty, the governors and viceroys of the provinces monopolized power, leading to the collapse of the imperial court. However, the monarchical system had not yet been replaced, and the minds of a group of people still held the dignity of an emperor, not daring to openly rebel in order to avoid the crime of treason. Therefore, although the facts were that the tail was wagging the dog, all appointments and removals still had to obey a central imperial order. After the founding of the Republic of China, warlords and politicians, who advertised republicanism and equality, acted arbitrarily. They had eliminated the human faith in their minds and had no concept of the entire country in their eyes. Those with real power only needed to increase the number of guns, and those in positions could say whatever they wanted. Today, it was one political view, and tomorrow, it was another territory. For more than ten years, our people have been in a state of deep water and scorching fire. The National Government is trusted by everyone to be able to implement Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Three Principles of the People and Five-Power Constitution, and to establish an organized, hopeful, and greatly developed country that can stand on its own and become strong. However, within it, political views are still incompatible, and military forces each hold their own territory. Some harshly criticize that the central government's decrees are not as extensive as Sun Chuanfang's era, which covered five provinces. What painful words these are! Let's put aside this nonsense for now. However, the sudden political upheavals and the phenomenon of dividing political power in various places after the establishment of the National Government have already been seen more than once. What has not yet been erased from our minds are the various actions of Wuhan, Northeast, Northwest, South, and Southwest, either openly forming separate governments or secretly seizing political power. I think that those officials currently serving under the banner of the central government should also have a sense of heartache. The first thing they have forgotten is the entire country. The second thing is that they are blinded by fame and fortune. The third thing is that they are surrounded by a group of politicians and have lost their direction. Therefore, they each have their own ideas, each has their own actions, each protects their own territory, and each expands their own power, creating a seemingly united but internally divided phenomenon. No wonder the Japanese repeatedly say at the League of Nations that we are an unorganized country. If you carefully interpret this criticism, isn't it saying that it's just a gathering of a chaotic mix of people who are like a bunch of drunkards and meat-eating brothers? Don't you think it's shameful? In the current central government, I firmly believe that there are quite a few people who have been abroad for a long time and have a clear understanding of the situation. However, it is inevitable that some people are swayed by others or have deeply ingrained habits. There are also those who know the broad road but occasionally get lost, and even those who use personal likes and dislikes as tools for political struggle. As a result, government orders have no target, and construction is difficult to progress. The establishment of the Central National Medicine Hall has already made us feel that there are strange rocks on the horizon. However, because it is an academic institution, and academic freedom of research is not prohibited in any country. Moreover, academics, especially practical subjects, not only rely on oral and written records, but also need to focus on materials and provide evidence. Therefore, successful research is an achievement, and without achievement, it is as if it does not exist. Let it be. Unexpectedly, recently, many important figures in the central government, I don't know what wire they suddenly touched, temporarily forgetting the national administrative organization and the consistent system of academics, and in a chaotic manner, wanted to give the Central National Medicine Hall, which has no basis, full political and academic power. They did not think that political power cannot be easily divided and that government orders cannot be arbitrarily given to others. They also did not think that within the Ministry of Education, which manages national culture, they could divide a portion of its political power and hand it over to the Central National Medicine Hall, which has no legal status. They also did not think that within the Ministry of Interior, which manages national civil affairs, they could divide a portion of its political power and hand it over to the Central National Medicine Hall, which has no legal status. Alas, what kind of national system is this? What kind of unified political and legal system is this? Isn't this the same as the separate establishment of governments and the expansion of their own labor force in Wuhan, Northeast, Northwest, South, and Southwest in the past? I would also like to ask the officials who proposed this: if this proposal is passed in the Legislative Yuan, will this group of Chinese medicine practitioners not be under the jurisdiction of the Executive Yuan, which governs the national politics of the central government, and will they not all become foreigners in our country? Have the officials who proposed this not made a mistake in their thinking? The Central National Medicine Hall cannot be regarded as the same as a foreign consulate. The day before yesterday, I read Jiao Yitang's letter to the nation published in the Capital Daily. In the end, it was all old news. He said that Western medicine focuses on materials, that Chinese medicine is good at treating diseases, that Chinese medicine theories cannot be expressed in formulas, but that its treatment results are still correct, that so-and-so's disease could not be cured by Western medicine but was cured by a certain doctor, that a certain important person deeply believed in Western medicine, so his carbuncle on his back has not healed, that the Ministry of Health has spent a lot of national funds, but cholera is still rampant, and that the living standards of Chinese people are not suitable for seeing Western doctors. In short, he advocates for the preservation of Chinese medicine. However, the preservation of Chinese medicine is entirely an academic issue. However, his article did make a mistake. The proposed National Medicine Regulations completely mixed academics and administration, and wanted to hand over this political power to the Central National Medicine Hall, which has no status in the administrative organization. How do you think this is possible? I think that the officials in the Legislative Yuan are well-versed in this type of administrative system organization and will not blindly follow. Taking a step back, if the officials in the Legislative Yuan also express their agreement, then, in order to avoid the suspicion of disrupting the administrative system, the following confirmations must be made first: (1) Establish the status of the Central National Medicine Hall so that it is subordinate to something. (2) The Central National Medicine Hall should remain an academic research institution and continue to exist as before. A separate Ministry of Medical Administration should be established, on par with other ministries, to specifically manage the administrative affairs of National Medicine. (3) The administrative aspects of National Medicine should be handed over to the Ministry of Interior to draft special articles. (4) The National Medicine Regulations should be handed over to the Department of Health to implement. In this way, National Medicine will first be subordinate to something, so that administrative measures can be based on something. Otherwise, the Legislative Yuan itself may also have inconveniences.

Common Sense Q&A on Diseases 202

— Cheng Hanzhang

(Author's Announcement) This column is a question-and-answer format and is not a correspondence question-and-answer service. Readers, please do not misunderstand and waste your time and postage by sending inquiries.

(14) Dysentery (A. Bacterial) Question: Is dysentery an infectious disease of the intestines? Answer: Yes. The pathogens of this disease also invade the intestinal tract.

Question: Dysentery can be divided into two types. One is called bacterial dysentery, which is caused by dysentery bacteria invading the large intestine. The other is amoebic dysentery, which is caused by dysentery amoebae invading the intestines. Question: How are the pathogenic bacteria of bacterial dysentery spread?

Answer: In summer or autumn, due to careless eating and drinking, items and foods containing viruses are eaten and invade the intestines, often spreading in a temporary epidemic. Question: How do these items and foods contain viruses?

Answer: All items that have been used by dysentery patients, or drinking water that has been contaminated by the excrement of patients, or food that has been touched by flies, contain viruses.

Question: How many days after infection with bacterial dysentery does it take to develop the disease? During this period, the patient does not feel anything, but there may be a loss of appetite, abdominal discomfort, and irregular bowel movements.

Question: What happens when the disease develops?

Answer: It starts with mild abdominal pain, accompanied by several episodes of diarrhea and a slight fever. Later, the number of bowel movements increases further, from several times to dozens of times a day. The stool loses its normal consistency and contains mucus, blood, or pus, and emits a foul odor. Usually, stools mixed with blood are called red dysentery, and stools containing mucus or pus are called white dysentery. Regardless of the number of bowel movements, each episode is only about ten to twenty grams. Before defecation, there is abdominal rumbling and colic, followed by a feeling of urgency (tenesmus).

Question: What is the patient's body temperature like?

Answer: The patient's body temperature rises slightly... If the affected area involves the lower section of the small intestine, then there will be a high fever, and even cerebral symptoms, very similar to typhoid fever. (To be continued)

Scientific Compilation of Achieving Longevity (Continued) 204
